## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration. In chemical kinetics, rate laws relate reaction rates to concentrations via power-law or more complex functional forms, with rate constants governing the speed.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions approaching equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction where product = c1 - A)
- Logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (autocatalysis with finite resources)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changing with time, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional-order kinetics with baseline rate)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy analog)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer-order rate laws → dA_dt proportional to A**n where n is 0, 1, 2, or 3 (most common reaction orders)
- Equilibrium/reversible reactions → rate expression as linear combination: c0*A + c1, where c1 represents back-reaction contribution from products
- Conservation of mass constraints → if total concentration is conserved, product concentration appears as (c - A), leading to polynomial expressions in A
- Enzyme/saturation kinetics → rational functions A/(c + A) indicating a limiting step or finite catalyst sites
- Autocatalytic behavior → product terms like A*(c - A) creating a quadratic in A with opposite-sign coefficients
- Absence of explicit time dependence → if dA/dt = f(A) only, the system is autonomous and rate law depends solely on current state
- Negative leading coefficient → indicates consumption/decay of species A (reactant being consumed)
- Stoichiometric coupling → when multiple species are linked by stoichiometry, their concentrations become linear functions of each other, reducing multi-species kinetics to functions of A alone

$$f(A) = \alpha \cdot A^2 + \frac{\beta \cdot A^2}{\gamma \cdot A^4 + 1}$$

where α = -0.18998, β = 0.45987, γ = 0.74980.

Now I need to check which candidates can match this form. Any candidate with `t` dependence must allow setting those terms to zero.

**Key structural requirement:** The GT has:
1. An A² term
2. A rational function A²/(A⁴+c) = A·[A/(A⁴+c)]

Note that A²/(A⁴·c + 1) can be rewritten. Let me factor: A²/(c·A⁴+1). If I write this as A·[A/(c·A⁴+1)], this is A times A/(c·A⁴+1).

Also note: A/(A²·c + 1) has a different structure - it's a rational function with A³ in denominator vs A⁵. So A·[A/(c·A²+1)] = A²/(c·A²+1) ≠ A²/(c·A⁴+1).

**Critical distinction:** Many candidates have the term `A*c1/(A²*c2 + 1)` which gives A/(A²+c), NOT A²/(A⁴+c). These are fundamentally different rational functions and cannot match.

Combining the two rational terms over a common denominator:
= c0·A² + A·[c1(c5·A²+1) + c4(c2·A²+1)] / [(c2·A²+1)(c5·A²+1)]
= c0·A² + A·[(c1·c5+c4·c2)A² + (c1+c4)] / [c2·c5·A⁴ + (c2+c5)A² + 1]

GT needs: c0·A² + β·A² / (γ·A⁴+1)

For the rational part: I need A·[(...)A²+(...)] / [c2c5·A⁴+(c2+c5)A²+1] to equal β·A²/(γ·A⁴+1).

This requires (c2+c5)=0, so c5=-c2. Then denominator = -c2²·A⁴+1 (need c2² negative for positive γ... but c2² is always positive). Actually γ=0.7498>0, so we need -c2²<0 which gives negative coefficient. That doesn't work since GT has +0.7498·A⁴.

Wait, let me reconsider. If c5=-c2, denominator = c2·(-c2)·A⁴ + 0·A² + 1 = -c2²·A⁴+1. We need this to equal γ·A⁴+1, so -c2² = γ = 0.7498, impossible for real c2.
